**Summary.** The researchers developed a new way to design optomechanical crystals that are attached to their substrate rather than suspended. By using an advanced inverse-design algorithm, they achieved extremely high light-matter coupling rates that rival suspended devices while preventing the device from overheating. This makes it a much more robust platform for quantum technologies.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides a scalable, thermally stable platform for quantum transducers and microwave-to-optical frequency conversion, which are essential for building large-scale quantum networks.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The trade-off in optomechanical crystals between high photon-phonon coupling strength and thermal robustness, where suspended structures provide high coupling but suffer from laser-induced heating.

**Main result.** The demonstration of a release-free silicon optomechanical crystal with a record vacuum coupling rate of 800 kHz, achieving performance comparable to suspended devices while maintaining superior thermal stability.

**Method.** A combination of the X-HOPE physics-guided technique to match wavevectors and a multiphysics gradient-based inverse-design algorithm using adjoint sensitivity analysis.

**Model / system.** A release-free silicon-on-insulator (220 nm Si on 2 um SiO2) optomechanical crystal architecture that is mechanically attached to the substrate to allow for efficient heat dissipation.

**Key observables.** Vacuum optomechanical coupling rate (g_OM), optomechanical scattering rate (Gamma_OM), optical quality factor (Q_o), and thermo-optic frequency shift.

**Important parameters / regimes.** g_OM/2pi approx 800 kHz, mechanical frequency 5.25 GHz, optical frequency 193.5 THz, and room-temperature operation.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The design assumes the ability to mitigate fabrication errors through stochastic erosion/dilation and focuses on radiation-limited performance as a benchmark.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows mode overlap and band structure for the X-HOPE design; Figure 2 illustrates the inverse-design algorithm workflow; Figure 3 presents experimental spectral data and coupling measurements; Figure 4 compares thermal stability across different architectures.

**Paper structure.** The paper identifies the optomechanical coupling/thermal trade-off, introduces the X-HOPE and inverse-design methodologies, details the experimental fabrication and measurement setup, presents the record-high coupling results, and concludes with a robustness analysis against fabrication imperfections.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Interactions between light and mechanics provide a powerful interface between optical and microwave-frequency signals, with applications spanning classical signal processing and quantum technologies. High-performance optomechanical devices require both strong photon-phonon coupling and tolerance to parasitic laser heating. Release-free optomechanical crystals provide improved thermal anchoring compared to suspended nanobeams, but have so far exhibited weaker vacuum optomechanical coupling rates, leaving a trade-off between coupling strength and thermal robustness. Here, we largely close this gap: we design and experimentally demonstrate a release-free silicon optomechanical crystal with a record vacuum optomechanical coupling rate of about $g_\text{OM} / (2 π) = 800$ kHz, comparable to suspended state-of-the-art devices. The resulting optomechanical scattering rate $Γ_\text{OM}/(2 π)= 1.1$ kHz is nearly twice that of previous release-free implementations. This performance is achieved by combining physics-guided human intuition with a multiphysics inverse-design algorithm introduced here for resonant optomechanical structures. Beyond the specific device demonstrated, the inverse-design framework is applicable to co-optimizing optical and mechanical resonances and eigenmodes more broadly. These results strengthen release-free optomechanical crystals as a platform for fast, low-noise classical and quantum optomechanics.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03132"></a>
### [A missing causal principle: Coordination](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03132v1)

**Authors:** Daniel Centeno, Antoine Coquet, Maria Ciudad Alañón, Lucas Tendick, Marc-Olivier Renou, Elie Wolfe  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03132v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03132_figures/2605.03132_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. Various causal structures represented as directed acyclic graphs (DAGs). Squares denote observed nodes and circles denote latent nodes. Latent nodes represent either sources of information (when parentless) or transformations of information (when they have parents), while observed nodes correspond to measurements. The label notation of the nodes is chosen to make causal relationships explicit. Concretely, we label latent nodes by the complement of the set of observed nodes in their future, denoted ¬(·), whereas the observed nodes are simply denoted by A1,...,AN. Reichenbach’s common cause principle rules out perfect coordination (indeed, any non-factorizing distribution) in (a),...</figcaption>
</figure>

<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> FIG. 2. Graphical representation of the quantum cut inflation of the two-layer tetrahedron. The superindex in parenthesis indicate the copy index of the sources in the past of the nodes. The black dots denote whenever the same Hilbert space of a given source state is pertinent in defining more than one transformation. Accordingly, pairs of transformations related by a black dot (i.e., ¬(A1A3)(1,1) and ¬(A1A3)(2,1) or ¬(A2A4)(1,1) and ¬(A2A4)(1,2)) cannot be physically implemented simultaneously. That implies incompatibility of their downstream measurements (A2 and A4 or A1 and A3, respectively). Nevertheless, while the whole quantum inflation is not physically valid, certain parts of it...</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03132_figures/2605.03132_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">

**Summary.** This paper introduces the Coordination Principle, stating that perfect agreement among multiple parties implies a shared common cause. It proves that quantum mechanics obeys this principle even in complex causal networks and provides new inequalities to experimentally certify common causes in multipartite GHZ states.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for researchers in quantum networks and quantum optics as it provides new experimental tools (Bell-like inequalities) to certify the existence of shared quantum resources and common causes in multipartite systems.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates whether the 'Coordination Principle'—the idea that perfect agreement on a random output among N parties requires a shared common cause—is a fundamental causal principle or merely a consequence of No-Signaling and Independence.

**Main result.** The authors prove that quantum theory satisfies the Coordination Principle in any causal network, even with intermediate transformations, and derive noise-tolerant Bell-like inequalities to certify the presence of a common cause.

**Method.** The study employs the 'Quantum Inflation' technique to expand causal structures, uses the NPA hierarchy for semidefinite programming, and constructs a counterexample using an Operational Probabilistic Theory (OPT) to show the principle is independent of No-Signaling.

**Model / system.** The framework uses Directed Acyclic Graphs (DAGs) to represent causal structures, specifically studying multipartite GHZ states and complex scenarios like the two-layer tetrahedron model.

**Key observables.** Correlations between adjacent parties (e.g., <Ai Ai+1>) and end-to-end correlations (e.g., <A1 AN>), as well as marginal probabilities.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The number of parties (N), the white noise visibility parameter (v), and the fidelity (f) of the GHZ state.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The proofs assume the use of pure states, unitary transformations, and projective measurements; it also assumes the possibility of device replication in certain contexts.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate various causal DAG structures, the quantum cut inflation construction, diagrammatic representations of tests and circuits in the counterexample OPT, and plots showing the violation of inequalities as a function of noise visibility.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the Coordination Principle, proves quantum theory satisfies it using inflation techniques, provides a counterexample OPT where the principle fails, derives noise-robust Bell-like inequalities, and applies these to GHZ state certification.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We introduce the coordination principle, which states that perfect coordination, in the form of agreement on a uniformly random output, among N parties is possible only if they share a common cause. This principle is purely causal and can be viewed as a multipartite generalization of Reichenbach's common cause principle. We prove that quantum information theory satisfy the coordination principle in any network, and derive noise-tolerant Bell-like inequalities that certify the presence of a common cause. We further show that the principle is not a consequence of no-signaling and independence alone by constructing a concrete operational probabilistic theory that obeys both principles while still allowing perfect coordination without a common cause. This possibility arises only in fully general causal scenarios with intermediate transformations between preparations and measurements. We also formulate a genuinely quantum coordination task, showing that the preparation of a multipartite GHZ state requires a quantum common cause, which can be certified by Bell-like inequalities which are experimentally testable. Finally, we discuss the open problem of finding a quantitative, noise-tolerant version of the coordination principle that constrains approximate coordination in any reasonable causal theory. This work is the extended version of the more compact letter and provides all the technical details of the proofs.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03605"></a>
### [Construction of a Non-Linear Entanglement Witness Operator in Arbitrary Dimension Using a Given Linear Witness Operator](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03605v1)

**Authors:** Sonia, Satyabrata Adhikari  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03605v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

**Summary.** This paper presents a method to transform standard linear entanglement witnesses into more powerful non-linear versions. These new operators can detect a wider range of entangled states, including difficult-to-identify positive partial transpose entangled states, and are designed to be implementable using local measurements.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is relevant for quantum information theorists as it provides a practical, experimentally realizable method to identify complex entanglement (like bound entanglement) that is otherwise invisible to standard linear detection methods.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The difficulty of detecting all types of entanglement, particularly Positive Partial Transpose Entangled States (PPTES), using traditional Linear Entanglement Witnesses (LEW) which often fail to detect certain entangled states.

**Main result.** The authors provide a systematic constructive approach to derive Non-Linear Entanglement Witnesses (NLEW) from existing LEWs, demonstrating that these NLEWs can detect a larger class of both NPTES and PPTES.

**Method.** A constructive mathematical framework using polynomial functional forms of LEWs, involving determinants, partial traces, and trace norms to transform linear operators into non-linear ones.

**Model / system.** Bipartite quantum systems in arbitrary dimensions (d1 x d2), with specific analyses performed on qubit-qubit (2x2), qubit-qutrit (2x3), and qutrit-qutrit (3x3) systems.

**Key observables.** Expectation value of the witness operator (Tr(W rho)), which indicates entanglement if negative.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Parameters defining specific state families such as alpha (isotropic states), p (LEW parameter), gamma (qutrit isotropic states), and x (qutrit PPTES parameter).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The construction assumes the existence of a known LEW and relies on the assumption that the maximum of a sum of expectation values is bounded by the sum of their individual maximums.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the functional form of NLEWs, provides specific constructions for NPTES, utilizes CCNR and De Vicente criteria for construction, presents a new method for PPTES detection, and concludes with a discussion on experimental realization via local observables.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Entanglement detection is one of the important problems in quantum information theory. To deal with this problem, many entanglement detection criteria have been proposed. Among the proposed criteria, the detection of entanglement through witness operator (also known as linear entanglement witness (LEW) operator) may be considered as the most practical. Although the witness operator approach to detect entanglement is experimentally friendly, the construction of these operators is not a very simple task. Even if we are able to construct a LEW operator, our problem is not solved as it may either detect a few entangled states or not a single entangled state from a given family of entangled states. Thus, we need a constructive approach in order to tackle this type of problem. In this work, we provide a few constructions of the non-linear entanglement witnesses (NLEW) for $d_1\otimes d_2$ dimensional system from any linear entanglement witness (LEW) operator. The advantage of these constructions is that, if a LEW is unable to detect any particular entangled state described by the density operator $ρ^{ent}$ then our construction of NLEW may detect the same entangled state $ρ^{ent}$. Further, we have constructed NLEW operator that may detect not only a class of bipartite negative partial transpose entangled state (NPTES), but also positive partial transpose entangled state (PPTES). Moreover, we have shown that the constructed NLEW operators may be decomposed in terms of the tensor product of local observables and hence may be realizable in an experiment.

</details>

### [Coordination Requires a Common Cause in Quantum Theory](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03120v1)

**Summary.** The paper demonstrates that in quantum theory, achieving perfect coordination among multiple parties is only possible if they share a common cause. It distinguishes quantum theory from other possible theories that satisfy standard causality principles but allow coordination without a common cause. Finally, it provides Bell-like inequalities to certify these common causes in noisy experimental settings.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant for quantum information and quantum optics as it establishes a new fundamental causal principle for quantum theory and provides practical, noise-robust tools for certifying multipartite entanglement and causal structures.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating whether the 'Coordination Principle'—the idea that perfect randomized coordination among multiple parties requires a common cause—is a fundamental property of quantum theory or merely a consequence of No-Signaling and Independence principles.

**Main result.** The authors prove that quantum theory satisfies the Coordination Principle, whereas other operational probabilistic theories satisfying No-Signaling and Independence do not. They also derive noise-tolerant Bell-like inequalities to experimentally certify the presence of a common cause.

**Method.** The authors use an Operational Probabilistic Theory (OPT) framework, employing a 'quantum inflation technique' and Sum of Squares (SOS) arguments to derive contradictions in circuits lacking a common cause.

**Model / system.** A network of N parties (specifically analyzed for N=4) connected via a causal circuit involving sources, intermediate channels, and measurement nodes, involving both classical bit coordination and quantum GHZ state generation.

**Key observables.** Correlators for bit agreement (e.g., p(a=b)) and fidelity of the 4-partite GHZ state.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Fidelity threshold (v > 94.17%) for certifying a quantum common cause in a noisy GHZ state.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The proof assumes that correlations in nature obey the mathematical structure of quantum theory and the Independence principle.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a causal circuit for a 4-party coordination task; Figure 2 illustrates the graphical representation of the quantum inflation process.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the Coordination Principle, constructs an OPT that violates it to show NSI is insufficient, proves the principle holds for quantum theory, extends it to quantum coordination tasks (GHZ states), and provides experimental certification tools via inequalities.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We propose a novel causal principle that is a genuinely multipartite extension of Reichenbach's common cause principle, namely, the coordination principle: parties in a network can achieve perfect randomized coordination--in particular, agree on a uniformly random output--only if they all share a common cause. We show that this principle does not follow from the standard no-signaling and independence principles by providing an explicit theory satisfying all these principles while violating the coordination principle. Strikingly, we prove that the coordination principle holds, however, in quantum theory for four parties, and derive noise-tolerant Bell-like inequalities that certify a common cause. We then extend these results to a genuinely quantum coordination task, showing that the four-partite GHZ state requires a quantum common cause which can also be certified by experimentally accessible Bell-like inequalities. A companion paper generalizes these results for N parties, proving that the coordination principle is satisfied in general for quantum theory.

</details>

### [Interplay of Nonstabilizerness and Ergotropy in Quantum Batteries](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03600v1)

**Summary.** This paper explores how the complexity of a quantum state, measured by its nonstabilizerness, relates to its capacity to store extractable work in a quantum battery. It finds that while a direct link exists under U(1) symmetry, this relationship disappears in more generic, symmetry-breaking dynamics. The study also demonstrates that high initial complexity is not required to achieve maximum charging power.

**Why it may be interesting.** It connects the resource theory of magic/nonstabilizerness to quantum thermodynamics, providing new insights into how quantum complexity affects the efficiency of energy storage and extraction in many-body systems.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the relationship between nonstabilizerness (magic) and the ability of quantum batteries to store and extract work (ergotropy).

**Main result.** A one-to-one correspondence between ergotropy and nonstabilizerness emerges in U(1)-symmetric interactions, whereas this link breaks in generic interactions; additionally, initial nonstabilizerness is not a necessary resource for optimal charging power.

**Method.** The authors use Stabilizer Renyi Entropy (SRE) to quantify nonstabilizerness and perform numerical simulations using XXZ spin chains, cSYK models, and random unitary circuits.

**Model / system.** A 1D chain of N spin-1/2 particles divided into a charger and a battery, utilizing interaction models such as the XXZ spin chain, the complex Sachdev-Ye-Kitaev (cSYK) model, and brick-wall random unitary circuits.

**Key observables.** Ergotropy (extractable work), nonstabilizerness (Stabilizer Renyi Entropy), stored energy, and charging power.

**Important parameters / regimes.** U(1) symmetry vs. symmetry-breaking interactions, system size N, circuit depth t, and the anisotropy parameter gamma.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis focuses on specific classes of unitary dynamics and assumes the use of SRE as a proxy for the complexity of the quantum state.

**Figures summary.** Figures show the growth and saturation of SRE and ergotropy over time, parametric plots showing functional relations (like tanh fits) between SRE and ergotropy, and data collapse of scaled quantities across different system sizes.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of nonstabilizerness in quantum batteries, analyzes U(1)-symmetric models (XXZ, cSYK), explores symmetry-breaking interactions via random circuits, and concludes by examining the impact of initial nonstabilizerness on charging power.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Nonstabilizerness plays an essential role in an efficient simulation of quantum systems on quantum computers. In this work, we investigate its role in the context of quantum batteries (QBs). To this end, we consider a system of N spin-1/2 particles, where the left half serves as the charger and the right half acts as the battery. By studying different classes of interactions between the charger and the battery, we quantify the amount of nonstabilizerness required to store work in the QB. Our results reveal that a one-to-one correspondence between the ergotropy stored in the battery and the total nonstabilizerness of the composite system emerges whenever the interaction Hamiltonian preserves a U(1) symmetry. In contrast, this correspondence is generally lost for more generic interactions that do not respect this symmetry. Finally, we examine the complementary scenario in which the battery is initialized in a nonstabilizer state and subsequently charged through Clifford evolution. In this case, we find that the maximum average charging power exhibits a non-monotonic dependence on the initial nonstabilizerness. Remarkably, the highest average power can be achieved even when the initial state carries no magic (nonstabilizerness), demonstrating that the initial magic is not a necessary resource for generating an optimal charging power in this protocol.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03518"></a>
### [Probing the robustness of various self-testing protocols for mulipartite entangled states](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03518v1)

**Authors:** Priyaranjan K. Jha, Ritesh K. Singh, A. K. Pan  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03518v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03518_figures/2605.03518_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. QρSn, Sn, (Sn)O  as a function of relative observed violation of the Svetlichny inequality for n = 3, 4, 5.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03518_figures/2605.03518_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> FIG. 2. QρMn, Mn, (Mn)O  as a function of relative observed viola- tion of the MABK inequality for n = 3, 4, 5.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper compares two different Bell-operator-based protocols for the device-independent certification of GHZ states. It finds that the Svetlichny-based protocol is much more resilient to noise than the MABK-based protocol. These results provide a practical guide for implementing robust multipartite entanglement verification in quantum networks.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant for researchers in quantum networks and quantum information as it identifies the most reliable method for certifying multipartite entanglement in realistic, noisy experimental settings.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the robustness of device-independent self-testing protocols for multipartite GHZ states against experimental imperfections like noise and finite statistics.

**Main result.** The study demonstrates that the Svetlichny-based self-testing protocol is significantly more robust than the MABK-based protocol, as it requires much lower Bell inequality violations to certify the state.

**Method.** The authors utilize the 'Self-Testing from Operator Inequality' (STOPI) framework, employing Jordan's lemma, matrix decomposition, and symmetry-based analytical techniques to derive linear lower bounds on extractable fidelity.

**Model / system.** The system consists of n-partite GHZ states shared among n spatially separated parties, where each party performs two dichotomic local measurements subject to a dephasing noise model.

**Key observables.** Extractable fidelity, Bell operator violations (Svetlichny and MABK), and the tradeoff function (extractability).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Number of parties (n=3, 4, 5), measurement angles (alpha), and the robustness scaling parameter (s).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes a device-independent scenario with two dichotomic measurements per party and a specific dephasing noise model.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the extractability for the Svetlichny protocol as a function of relative violation for n=3, 4, 5; Figure 2 shows the corresponding decrease in extractability for the MABK protocol.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of self-testing robustness, defines the Bell operators and noise models, applies the STOPI framework using operator inequalities, provides explicit analytical proofs for n=3, 4, and 5, and concludes with a comparison of protocol performance.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Device-independent certification of multipartite entangled states plays a central role   in a wide range of practical applications, including quantum networks, conference key agreement, and verifiable distributed quantum computation. A particularly important class of multipartite entangled states is the class of Greenberger-Horne-Zeilinger (GHZ) states. Many Bell operators have been proposed to self-test GHZ states. However, in practical scenarios, due to imperfections and the finite collection of statistics, the observed statistics do not satisfy the ideal self-testing relations. Hence, it becomes essential to investigate and compare the robustness of the different self-testing protocols. In this work, we investigate the robustness of self-testing schemes constructed from Bell operators due to Svetlichny and Mermin--Ardehali--Belinskii--Klyshko (MABK), using the analytic operator-inequality framework developed by Kaniewski [\href{https://doi.org/10.1103/PhysRevLett.117.070402}{Phys. Rev. Lett. 117, 070402 (2016)}]. We derive lower bounds on the extractable fidelity as a function of the observed value of these Bell operators. Although these protocols self-test the same underlying state, they exhibit markedly different levels of robustness. By comparing the resulting fidelity bounds, we demonstrate that the self-testing scheme based on the Svetlichny's Bell operator is the more robust among the two. Our results thus identify the Svetlichny operator based self-testing protocol as the most favorable candidate for device-independent certification of GHZ states in realistic, noisy experimental scenarios.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.03121"></a>
### [Simulation-guided design of an integrated photonic cavity for frequency-multiplexed Spontaneous Parametric Down Conversion](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03121v1)

**Authors:** Benjamin Szamosfalvi, Michael Raymer, CJ Xin, Leticia Magalhaes, Jarrett Nelson, Marko Lončar, Ryan M. Camacho  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03121v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `interference shaping light` **3/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03121_figures/2605.03121_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Figure 1. 3D illustration of the proposed photonic microresonator structure with SPDC modes and their coupling in and out of the resonator highlighted.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03121_figures/2605.03121_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">

Negligible overlaps between the modes at 1550 nm indicate very low coupling between the racetrack and pulley waveguides. The modes were solved for at the apex of the pulley coupler bend.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03121_figures/2605.03121_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">

Component simulations produce scattering-parameter matrices that feed the circuit simulator, which returns the cavity spectrum. Those extracted cavity parameters are then used to calculate the predicted JSA and PGR.</figcaption>

In the contour plots, the rows correspond to a broadband pump of σf = 100 GHz ((a), (b), (c)) and a narrowband pump ((d), (e), (f)) of σf = 5 GHz, while the columns represent low Qs of Qlow ≈103 ((a), (d)) and high Qs of Qhigh ≈105 ((c), (f)). Plot (b) shows a vertical cross-section (constant ωs) for the broad pump regime, demonstrating how the frequency state has undesirable side-islands, though the probability density in the side islands is smaller by several orders of magnitude. </figure>

**Summary.** The paper presents a design strategy for integrated photonic resonators that uses classical electromagnetic simulations to predict quantum entanglement properties. By optimizing a lithium niobate racetrack resonator, the authors demonstrate the ability to support a large number of frequency-entangled photon-pair modes with high efficiency. This approach allows for the pre-fabrication optimization of high-performance sources for quantum networking.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a powerful predictive framework for engineering high-dimensional frequency-entangled states, which are essential for scalable quantum networks and frequency-domain quantum information processing.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Designing integrated photonic cavity sources for frequency-multiplexed SPDC that simultaneously achieve high pair generation efficiency, narrow bandwidths, and high mode counts for quantum networking.

**Main result.** A simulated TFLN racetrack resonator design achieving 90 doubly resonant frequency-mode pairs with an effective Schmidt number of 89.62 and a total internal pair-generation-rate efficiency of 1.16 GHz/mW.

**Method.** A simulation pipeline combining classical full-wave electromagnetic simulations (FDTD, EME) with a new analytical framework that maps classical cavity parameters to quantum Joint Spectral Amplitude (JSA).

**Model / system.** An integrated photonic racetrack resonator on a thin-film lithium niobate (TFLN) platform utilizing Type-0 spontaneous parametric down-conversion (SPDC) in a periodically poled waveguide.

**Key observables.** Joint Spectral Amplitude (JSA), Joint Spectral Intensity (JSI), Schmidt number, Pair Generation Rate (PGR) efficiency, and Integrated Brightness Enhancement Factor (IBEF).

**Important parameters / regimes.** 90 resonant mode pairs, 1.08 GHz average bandwidth, 51.9 GHz Free Spectral Range (FSR), and high-Q regime (Q approx 1.78e5).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Uses a first-order perturbative SPDC model; assumes negligible multi-photon production; neglects small extra terms in the nonlinear interaction coefficient; assumes all interacting modes are in the fundamental TE mode.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the resonator structure; Figure 2 shows waveguide modes and coupler supermodes; Figure 4 shows JSA contour plots; Figure 7/8 show trade-offs between PGR and Q-factor; Figure 9/10/11 detail IBEF scaling and EME simulation accuracy.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the need for multiplexed sources, presents a new analytical-classical simulation pipeline, details the TFLN racetrack design and optimization, quantifies quantum performance metrics (JSA, Schmidt number), and concludes with a theoretical derivation of brightness enhancement.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Frequency-multiplexed entangled photon pair sources with narrow bandwidths and high pair generation efficiency are a key enabling technology for quantum networking. We present a simulation-based design study of an integrated photonic racetrack resonator source for spontaneous parametric down-conversion (SPDC) that simultaneously achieves all three properties. The central result is a simulated set of 90 doubly resonant signal/idler frequency-mode pairs with an effective Schmidt number of 89.62, average bandwidths of 1.08 GHz, a mean free spectral range of 51.9 GHz, and a total internal pair-generation-rate efficiency of 1.16 GHz/mW. Under deterministic wavelength-based splitting, the accessible frequency-state Schmidt number is reduced to 44.93. To support these predictions, we derive a closed-form analytical connection between classical cavity parameters (resonant frequencies, decay rates, coupling coefficients) and the quantum joint spectral amplitude and pair generation rate, extending the dispersive-medium quantization formalism of Raymer to the nonlinear optical cavity case. We demonstrate how classical electromagnetic field simulations can be combined with this analytical framework to predict quantum figures of merit for an integrated photonic source prior to fabrication. Fabrication and experimental validation are left for future work.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03104"></a>
### [Strong Locality as a Tetrahedron: A Symmetry-Reduced Geometric Representation of the (3,3,2,2) Bell Scenario](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03104v1)

**Authors:** Marek Gazdzicki, Francesco Giacosa, Pawel Piesowicz  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03104v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03104_figures/2605.03104_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Figure 1: Light-cone diagram for two sites, (q1, a1) and (q2, a2) and their corresponding past domains, Γ1</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03104_figures/2605.03104_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Figure 2: Geometry of the strongly-local models in the symmetry-reduced mixed-moment space (X, Y, Z). Left: The curved closed surface forms the boundary of the Nλ = 1 factorisable models parametrised by X = αβ, Y = αγ, Z = βγ with |α|, |β|, |γ| ≤1. It consists of the six hyperbolic faces arising from the boundaries |α| = 1, |β| = 1, and |γ| = 1 (each shown in a different colour). The four red points mark the extremal deterministic configurations. Right: Convex mixtures of such models generate the full set of SL models, which forms the regular tetrahedron with vertices (1, 1, 1), (−1, −1, 1), (−1, 1, −1), and (1, −1, −1). The planar faces of the tetrahedron correspond to the three...</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03104_figures/2605.03104_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Figure 3: Geometric relation between the strongly-local, quantum, and no-signalling sets of models in the symmetry-reduced conditional mixed-moment space (X, Y, Z). The SL region forms a regular tetrahedron (blue), and the quantum region appears as a larger curved convex body (red elliptope surface) defined by 1 + 2XY Z −X2 −Y 2 −Z2 ≥0, and the no-signalling region is the surrounding cube [−1, 1]3 (green dashed edges). After projection onto the three mixed moments, all non-trivial no-signalling facet inequalities disappear, so the no-signalling models occupy the entire cube.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** The paper simplifies the complex 36-dimensional (3,3,2,2) Bell scenario into a 3D geometric representation where the strongly-local region is a simple tetrahedron. This reduction reveals a clear nested hierarchy between strongly-local, quantum, and no-signaling models and offers a more pronounced separation of these sets than the standard CHSH case.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a highly simplified geometric visualization of the hierarchy of quantum correlations and introduces a 'diagonal-free' testing method that avoids experimental loopholes like detection efficiency or particle bunching.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Characterizing the geometric structure of strongly-local models in the high-dimensional (3,3,2,2) Bell scenario by reducing its complexity.

**Main result.** The authors show that in a symmetry-reduced 3D mixed-moment space, the strongly-local region forms a regular tetrahedron (the 'pyramid') defined by only three linear inequalities, embedded within a quantum elliptope and a no-signaling cube.

**Method.** Symmetry reduction using site indistinguishability and projection of the 36-dimensional Bell polytope onto a 3D space of off-diagonal mixed moments (X, Y, Z).

**Model / system.** A bipartite Bell scenario with two spatially separated, indistinguishable sites, each having three measurement settings and two binary outcomes.

**Key observables.** Conditional mixed moments (products of outcomes for off-diagonal measurement settings) X, Y, and Z.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Three measurement settings per site (0, 1, 2) and binary outcomes (+1, -1).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The two measurement sites are indistinguishable (exchange symmetry) and measurement settings are independent of hidden variables.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a light-cone diagram of the bipartite setup; Figure 2 illustrates the boundary of factorizable models and the resulting SL tetrahedron; Figure 3 depicts the nested hierarchy of the SL tetrahedron, the quantum elliptope, and the no-signaling cube.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the (3,3,2,2) scenario, applies symmetry reduction to a 3D mixed-moment space, derives the geometric shapes and inequalities for the SL, Q, and NS regions, and compares the results to the standard CHSH case.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We present a geometric characterisation of strongly-local models in the bipartite Bell scenario with three measurement settings per site and binary outcomes, i.e.\ the (3,3,2,2) case. Restricting attention to indistinguishable sites, we introduce a three-dimensional mixed-moment space in which the mixed moments are calculated under off-diagonal measurement settings.   In this reduced representation, the strongly-local region assumes the remarkably simple form of a regular tetrahedron - the 'pyramid'. We prove that only three independent linear inequalities are required to characterise this region. We call them the pyramid inequalities that separate strongly-local ($\mathcal{SL}$) models from their complement, non-strongly-local ($\mathcal{\overline{SL}}$) models. We also clarify the relation between the symmetry-reduced pyramid representation and the full (3,3,2,2) Bell polytope in the 36-dimensional conditional-probability space, which possesses 684 facet-defining inequalities. The reduction from 684 to three reflects normalisation, symmetry reduction, and projection to the mixed-moment space.   In the pyramid representation, the hierarchy $\mathcal{SL} \subsetneq \mathcal{Q} \subsetneq \mathcal{NS}$ appears geometrically as a tetrahedron embedded in a somewhat larger curved body of quantum models, $\mathcal{Q}$, which in turn is embedded in a cube of no-signalling models, $\mathcal{NS}$. The qualitative and quantitative advantages of the pyramid representation over the standard CSHS representation for the (2,2,2,2) case are discussed.

</details>

### [Relations between different definitions of the quantum Wasserstein distance for qubits](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03027v1)

**Authors:** Géza Tóth, József Pitrik  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03027v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03027_figures/2605.03027_page3.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 3</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 5</figcaption>

</div>

**Summary.** This paper proves that two different definitions of quantum Wasserstein distance are identical for qubits when using a single operator in the cost function. It further demonstrates that this equivalence allows the ground state energy of certain spin chains to be expressed directly via the Wigner-Yanase skew information.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is relevant for researchers in quantum information and many-body dynamics as it establishes a fundamental link between quantum optimal transport metrics and information-theoretic quantities like the Wigner-Yanase skew information.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the relationship between two different definitions of the quantum Wasserstein distance for qubits: the DGMPC definition and the DPT definition.

**Main result.** The authors prove that for qubits, the DPT and DGMPC distances are equivalent when the cost function involves a single operator, and they show that the self-distance in this case equals the Wigner-Yanase skew information.

**Method.** The study uses quantum optimal transport theory, involving optimization over bipartite density matrices (couplings) with fixed marginals, and employs unitary transformations to simplify the operators into real matrices.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on two-level quantum systems (qubits) and considers the context of ferromagnetic spin chains.

**Key observables.** Quantum Wasserstein distances (D_DPT and D_DGMPC), Wigner-Yanase skew information, Quantum Fisher Information, and ground state energy of spin chains.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The case where the cost function contains a single operator (N=1).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The proven equivalence is specifically restricted to qubits and the case of a single operator in the cost function.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by defining the two Wasserstein distance frameworks, introduces a lemma for unitary rotation to real matrices, provides a proof for the equivalence theorem for qubits, and concludes by relating the results to the ground state energy of spin chains.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

The quantum Wasserstein distances defined by Golse, Mouhot, Paul, and Caglioti and by De Palma and Trevisan coincide for qubits when a single operator appears in the cost function. As a consequence, the self-distance equals the Wigner-Yanase skew information in this case.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03864"></a>
### [The power of entanglement in distributed quantum machine learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03864v1)

**Authors:** Yerim Kim, Kiwmann Hwang, Hyukjoon Kwon, Yosep Kim  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03864v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5**

**Summary.** This paper investigates how entanglement can be used to overcome communication delays in distributed quantum machine learning. It demonstrates that while entanglement boosts classification accuracy, there is an optimal amount to use to avoid reducing the model's parameter space. This research offers a pathway for scalable quantum computing across distant nodes.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a link between nonlocality (CHSH-like correlations) and machine learning advantage, offering a strategy to perform distributed computations despite coherence-time constraints.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Addressing the issue of communication latency in distributed quantum computing, which can exceed qubit coherence times, by using entanglement as a resource.

**Main result.** Entanglement improves classification accuracy in distributed quantum machine learning for binary tasks, though excessive entanglement can degrade performance by reducing the effective parameter space dimension.

**Method.** The study examines distributed quantum machine learning for binary classification, drawing an analogy between entanglement utility and the CHSH game.

**Model / system.** A distributed quantum machine learning framework for binary classification tasks involving remote nodes connected via entanglement.

**Key observables.** Classification accuracy and the effective dimension of the parameter space.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Amount and structure of entanglement in data embedding; communication latency/delay scales.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Entanglement can be established beforehand to mitigate the effects of latency during computation.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of latency in the quantum internet, proposes entanglement as a solution, analyzes its impact on distributed machine learning accuracy, and discusses the optimization of entanglement structure.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

The quantum internet aims to interconnect distant devices and enable large-scale computation through distributed quantum algorithms. One of the key obstacles is communication latency during computation. Even separations of a few hundred kilometers introduce millisecond-scale delays, which exceed the coherence times of many solid-state qubit platforms. In contrast, entanglement can be established beforehand and used as a practical resource to reduce communication complexity between remote nodes. Here we examine the utility of entanglement in distributed quantum machine learning for binary classification tasks. Drawing an analogy with the CHSH game, we show that entanglement improves classification accuracy across all datasets considered. We also find that excessive entanglement may degrade performance by reducing the effective dimension of the parameter space. This highlights the importance of using an appropriate amount and structure of entanglement in data embedding. Our findings bridge nonlocality and machine-learning advantage, providing a pathway toward distributed quantum computation beyond coherence-time constraints.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03381"></a>
### [Nonlinear semigroups with unbounded generators under Carleman linearization](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03381v1)

**Authors:** Sitanshu Gakkhar, Ala Shayeghi, David C. Del Rey Fernández  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** numerical methods · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03381v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **2/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03381_figures/2605.03381_page2.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 2</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03381_figures/2605.03381_page3.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 3</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03381_figures/2605.03381_page4.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 4</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03381_figures/2605.03381_page5.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 5</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03381_figures/2605.03381_page6.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 6</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper provides a rigorous functional analytic framework for the convergence of Carleman linearization, particularly for systems with unbounded operators. It replaces restrictive norm-based convergence conditions with more flexible dissipativity constraints. This allows for the valid approximation of complex nonlinear PDEs using higher-order linear hierarchies.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for researchers developing quantum algorithms for nonlinear dynamics, as it provides a rigorous mathematical foundation for the convergence of Carleman-based classical simulations of nonlinear systems.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Establishing the convergence and well-posedness of Carleman linearization for nonlinear evolutionary equations, especially when the underlying operators are unbounded, such as in discretized partial differential equations.

**Main result.** The authors prove that the convergence of truncated Carleman hierarchies can be reduced to the convergence of the Trotter-Kato approximation and establish conditions for the generation of C0-semigroups and 1-integrated semigroups using dissipativity constraints.

**Method.** The study employs the approximation theory of strongly continuous semigroups, the Trotter-Kato approximation theorem, and Lumer-Phillips theorem, treating the nonlinear dynamics as a linear system on a free Fock space.

**Model / system.** Nonlinear polynomial evolutionary equations of the form phi' = W1*phi + W2*phi^2, with specific applications to the hyperviscous Burgers' equation and reaction-diffusion type equations.

**Key observables.** The solution u(t) to the nonlinear equation, recovered by projecting the solution of the linearized system onto the first tensor factor.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The Carleman truncation level N, the nonlinearity parameter R, the dissipativity of the linear operator W1, and the relative A-bound of the perturbation.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Assumes the linear part W1 is a closed, densely defined, and dissipative operator; requires the generators to be closable; and assumes certain kernel inclusions for the nonlinear terms.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by defining the Carleman embedding in Fock space, moves to establishing convergence via Trotter-Kato and dissipativity analysis, addresses the unbounded operator regime using relative boundedness, and concludes with specific examples like the hyperviscous Burgers' equation.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We treat the convergence of Carleman linearization of nonlinear evolutionary equations through the approximation theory of strongly continuous semigroups, by Carleman embedding the underlying nonlinear semigroups as linear semigroups. Linear semigroup theory then lets one replace the norm constraint on the convergence of Carleman linearization in the form used by quantum algorithms for a class of semi-discretized evolution equations by a dissipativity constraint, simplifying arguments for convergence. Applying Trotter-Kato approximation theorem to the linearized semigroup realizes the semigroup as a limit finite dimensional operator exponentials, reducing the question of convergence rate of Carleman linearization to that of the Trotter-Kato approximation. We then examine convergence of the Carleman linearization as the operators become unbounded, treating the hyperviscuous Burger's equation as an example. Next we consider the perturbation theory of the Carleman semigroup and obtain conditions when polynomial nonlinearities correspond to the Carleman linearized semigroup being a $1$-integrated semigroup, so convergence is implied by variants of Trotter-Kato approximation for integrated semigroups.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.03829"></a>
### [A Berry-Esseen Bound for Quantum Lattice Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03829v1)

**Authors:** Marcus Cramer, Fernando G. S. L. Brandão, Mădălin Guţă, Álvaro M. Alhambra, Matteo Scandi  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03829v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `analog quantum simulation` **2/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03829_figures/2605.03829_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Figure 1. Representation of the operators defined in Eq. (62). Each b Hℓ j(m) corresponds to the terms in the Hamiltonian that are in the m-th layer (of width 2Rℓ) starting from j. On the other hand, zℓ j(m) corresponds to the remaining Hamiltonian when m layers have been discarded.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper provides a rigorous Berry-Esseen bound for quantum lattice systems, quantifying how quickly the distribution of local observables approaches a Gaussian. It shows that for systems with decaying correlations, the convergence error scales nearly as N^{-1/2}, providing an optimal rate for finite-size quantum systems.

**Why it may be interesting.** This provides a rigorous foundation for the Central Limit Theorem in many-body dynamics, offering precise error bounds that are crucial for understanding the validity of Gaussian approximations in large-scale quantum simulations and thermodynamic limits.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Establishing a rigorous Berry-Esseen bound for quantum lattice systems to quantify the rate of convergence of local observable statistics toward a normal distribution.

**Main result.** The authors prove that for large but finite quantum lattice systems, the distribution of local observables (like energy) approaches a Gaussian with an error scaling as O(N^{-1/2} polylog(N)), which is optimal up to logarithmic factors.

**Method.** The proof utilizes Esseen's inequality, characteristic functions, and a differential equation approach, combined with a peeling procedure and truncated Taylor expansions to manage non-commuting local operators.

**Model / system.** Quantum lattice systems with N particles/sites and a local (R-local) Hamiltonian consisting of bounded operators, where the quantum state exhibits decaying spatial correlations (exponential or polynomial).

**Key observables.** Local observables such as energy or magnetization.

**Important parameters / regimes.** System size N, lattice dimension D, correlation decay rate (alpha), locality radius R, and the variance of the Hamiltonian.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The quantum state must have sufficiently fast decaying correlations, the Hamiltonian must be local and bounded, and the variance must scale linearly with the system size.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates the partitioning of the Hamiltonian into concentric layers based on distance from an anchor point.

**Paper structure.** The paper establishes the setting of local Hamiltonians and decaying correlations, defines the Berry-Esseen figure of merit, uses Esseen's inequality to transform the problem into a characteristic function analysis, and employs a differential equation and operator decomposition strategy to bound the error terms.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

It is expected that the statistical fluctuations of local observables in large quantum systems obey the central limit theorem, and approximate a normal distribution as their size grows. Here, we prove a version of the Berry-Esseen theorem for quantum lattice systems, which strengthens that central limit theorem by providing a rigorous convergence estimate towards the normal distribution for large but finite system size. Given a local quantum Hamiltonian on $N$ particles and a quantum state with a finite correlation length, the result states that the measurement of local observables such as the energy follows a normal distribution, up to an error scaling as $\mathcal{O}\left(N^{-\frac{1}{2}} \text{polylog}(N)\right)$, which is optimal up to logarithmic factors.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.03612"></a>
### [A Critical Comment on 'Entropy Computing: A Paradigm for Optimization in Open Photonic Systems'](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03612v1)

**Authors:** Ali Hamed Moosavian, Bahram Abedi Ravan  
**Type:** both · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03612v1>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Figure 4: The number of configurations that correspond to a certain cut value, averaged over 1000 random graphs with 30 nodes, 233 edges and Max-Cut value 146, Max-3-Cut value of at least 191 and Max-4-Cut value of at least 210. The error bars are one standard deviation.</figcaption>
</figure>

</div>

**Summary.** This paper challenges the claim that 'Entropy Quantum Computing' offers a new computational advantage by showing that its performance on optimization tasks is matched or exceeded by standard classical metaheuristics. The authors argue that the Dirac-3 system acts as a physically motivated classical heuristic rather than a fundamentally new quantum paradigm.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a rigorous critique of a proposed new computing paradigm by applying tools from statistical mechanics and complexity theory to assess whether environmental noise can truly be leveraged for quantum advantage.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper critically evaluates the claims of computational advantage in 'Entropy Quantum Computing' (EQC) implemented via the Dirac-3 photonic system, specifically investigating if it outperforms state-of-the-art classical optimization algorithms.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that the Dirac-3 system's performance on Max-Cut and non-convex optimization problems does not exceed modern classical metaheuristics like PSO, ECA, or Simulated Annealing, and that its observed successes can be explained by classical stochastic sampling.

**Method.** The authors use numerical replication of the original benchmarks, implementation of classical metaheuristics in Julia, and theoretical analysis of the system's performance against known algorithmic bounds (e.g., Goemans-Williamson).

**Model / system.** The system is the Dirac-3, an open photonic platform using an optical-feedback loop with an amplifier, mixer, and loss medium to simulate imaginary time evolution and sample from a Boltzmann distribution.

**Key observables.** Cut values (Max-k-Cut), success rates, frequency distributions of cut sizes, and effective inverse temperature (beta).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Low mean photon numbers (weak coherent states), effective temperature (beta), and the number of nodes (n) in random graphs.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes the validity of the Unique Games Conjecture for establishing baselines and relies on the approximation that the system behaves as a Gibbs sampler.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the Dirac-3 schematic; Figure 2 illustrates the convergence of classical metaheuristics to a global minimum; Figure 5 shows the fit between the Boltzmann distribution model and experimental measurements.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins with a critique of the EQC paradigm, followed by a benchmarking of the Dirac-3 against modern classical solvers, a theoretical investigation of its performance on random graphs relative to approximation bounds, and a concluding assessment of its status as a heuristic rather than a new computing paradigm.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

In this article, we take a close look at Entropy Quantum Computing (EQC), a computational paradigm developed by Quantum Computing Inc. (QCi), which deviates from mainstream quantum computing by embracing rather than battling environmental noise and decoherence arXiv:2407.04512 . In their words this approach purports EQC as an open quantum system that turns "entropy into super-power fuels of its computing engine". We show that some of the claims in the main article can be made more rigorous, and yet these are still not good enough to beat state of the art classical algorithms on conventional classical computers. Note that these conclusions reflect the technology's current early stage of development and are not meant to discourage its pursuit. Continued rigorous exploration is necessary to fully assess the long-term viability and potential advantages of this distinct computational approach.

</details>

### [Fault-tolerant measurement-device-independent quantum key distribution with noisy non-Gaussian error correction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03292v1)

**Authors:** Zhiyue Zuo, Stefano Pirandola  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03292v1>

**Summary.** The study proposes a fault-tolerant CV-MDI-QKD protocol using GKP error correction to overcome the range limitations of current continuous-variable networks. By using non-Gaussian codes and a concatenation strategy, the researchers show that both loss and noise can be suppressed, significantly extending the secure communication distance in both fiber and wireless settings.

**Why it may be interesting.** This paper is highly relevant to quantum optics and open quantum systems as it demonstrates how non-Gaussian error correction (GKP codes) can be used to combat Gaussian noise and loss in bosonic channels, a central theme in developing robust quantum networks.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The limited secure transmission range of continuous-variable measurement-device-independent quantum key distribution (CV-MDI-QKD) due to sensitivity to loss and additive Gaussian noise.

**Main result.** The proposed GKP-based error correction scheme suppresses both loss and operation errors below the break-even point, extending the maximum secure transmission distance in both fiber and free-space links.

**Method.** An enhanced asymmetric CV-MDI-QKD protocol using Gottesman-Kitaev-Preskill (GKP) oscillator-to-oscillator codes and a one-by-one concatenation method to extract error syndromes via ancilla measurements.

**Model / system.** An asymmetric CV-MDI-QKD network topology featuring an untrusted relay connecting Alice and Bob, utilizing coherent states, GKP ancilla modes, and Two-Mode Squeezed (TMS) operations across fiber and wireless (fading) channels.

**Key observables.** Secret key rate (asymptotic and composable finite-size), residual error variance, mutual information, and Holevo information.

**Important parameters / regimes.** GKP squeezing levels (e.g., 20 dB), channel transmittance, fiber attenuation (0.2 dB/km), and number of concatenation layers.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Security is analyzed against collective Gaussian attacks using the quantum de Finetti theorem; the use of a linear estimation function for error syndromes instead of MMSE.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the network topology and protocol schematic; Figure 2 compares key rates against the PLOB bound; Figure 3 illustrates the GKP error correction architecture and residual error variance; Figure 5 shows RCI and finite-size key rates for ideal and noisy GKP states; Figure 6 shows the PDF of error variance in fading channels.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the CV-MDI-QKD limitation, proposes a GKP-based error correction scheme using TMS operations, provides a detailed security analysis under collective attacks, evaluates performance in fiber and free-space (fading) channels, and discusses the optimization of concatenated layers.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

It is well known that the repeater node is an essential ingredient for the future global quantum network, which will enable high-rate private communication and entanglement distribution over very long distances. The near-term repeater architecture uses the measurement-based node that operate without both entanglement and quantum memory, which is the main idea of the measurement-device-independent quantum key distribution (MDI-QKD) protocol. The MDI-QKD protocol removes the trust condition from the inter repeaters, while its continuous variable (CV) version, when proposed, benefited from its deterministic nature, compatible with the classical devices, and shows a high rate for the short-range local area network (LAN). Whilst the theoretical backbone of CV-MDI-QKD protocol is well established, its secure transmission range is yet limited for practical LAN. In this study, we propose an enhanced scheme for the asymmetric CV-MDI-QKD protocol by using Gottesman-Kitaev-Preskill (GKP) oscillators-to-oscillators codes, where both loss error and operation error are suppressed to below the break-even point, without any delays caused by classical heralding signals. In particular, the proposed scheme, which correlates the noises of the data and ancilla via a pair of symplectic transforms, extracts the error syndromes from stabilizer measurements on the ancilla mode and informs the data mode for a corrective displacement. Numerical analysis shows the composable finite-size security of the protocol under the collective Gaussian attack, encompassing noiseless and noisy GKP states, with both wired (i.e., fiber-based) and wireless (i.e., free-space) configurations. In addition, we demonstrate that the residual errors of the GKP code can be further reduced by the concatenation method but has a trade-off between the layers number and the finite GKP squeezing.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.03191"></a>
### [Non-Markovian entropy production fluctuation theorem driven by a time-dependent electric field](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03191v1)

**Authors:** K. S. Rodríguez-Vigil, M. A. Bastarrachea-Magnani, J. I. Jiménez-Aquino  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03191v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03191_figures/2605.03191_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.03191_figures/2605.03191_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">

Panels (e–h) correspond to Ω= 1.5, where (e-f) present the average work and (g-h) the total entropy production for the same ordering.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper proves that the Detailed Fluctuation Theorem holds for a non-Markovian system driven by an electric field that affects both the particle and the bath. It shows that the standard fluctuation-dissipation theorem remains valid even when an induced electric force is present. The study highlights how memory effects can lead to temporary energy backflow and negative entropy production.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the validity of the Detailed Fluctuation Theorem (DFT) for total entropy production in a non-Markovian system driven by a time-dependent electric field.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that Kubo's second fluctuation-dissipation theorem remains unchanged despite induced electric forces, and prove the validity of the Detailed Fluctuation Theorem for total entropy production.

**Method.** The study uses the Zwanzig-Caldeira-Leggett model, Generalized Langevin Equations, and Laplace transforms to solve for the system's dynamics and probability density.

**Model / system.** A Brownian particle with charge Q in a harmonic potential, embedded in a charged fluid bath of harmonic oscillators, subjected to a time-dependent electric field.

**Key observables.** Total entropy production, average work, dissipated heat, and Gaussian probability density of position.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Electric field frequency (Omega), friction memory correlation time (tau_c), friction coefficient (gamma_0), and the overdamped vs. underdamped regimes.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is initially in thermal equilibrium, the potential is harmonic, and the induced force is approximated based on high-frequency bath oscillations.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the time behavior of the system in the overdamped regime under weak and high-frequency driving.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins with the derivation of the Generalized Langevin Equation from a Hamiltonian, proceeds to solve for the probability density and verify FDT invariance, then analyzes entropy production and work statistics, and concludes with the derivation of the Markovian limit.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Fluctuation theorems are key to understanding both fundamental and applied aspects of non-equilibrium thermodynamics of small systems. We study the non-Markovian entropy production fluctuation theorem for the diffusion process of charged particles in a gas inside a harmonic potential and under the action of a time-dependent electric field, using a generalized Langevin equation. By considering the influence of the electric field on both the tagged Brownian particle and the bath particles, an "induced" electric force arises. Despite the additional force, we demonstrate that Kubo's second fluctuation-dissipation theorem (FDT) remains unchanged. The FDT allows us to obtain the Gaussian probability density for the position along a single stochastic trajectory, which is the key to demonstrating the validity of the detailed fluctuation theorem (DFT) for the total entropy production. We study the specific result of an Ornstein-Uhlenbeck-type friction memory kernel and an oscillating electric field, and analyze the average work and entropy production in different parameter regimes.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.04021"></a>
### [Quantum work beyond classical (commuting) limits](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04021v1)

**Authors:** Sumit Rout, Aravinth Balaji Ravichandran, Paweł Horodecki, Anubhav Chaturvedi  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.04021v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.04021_figures/2605.04021_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. Work-extraction task. A pure preparation |ψx⟩is supplied to a single work device, while the source side is constrained only by pairwise maximal-energy constraints under one common normalized Hamiltonian. The device is queried through a bounded Hamiltonian setting 0 ≤Hy ≤I and may use an arbitrary thermodynamic protocol involving a heat bath, internal control, and work storage. Each run realizes one branch of the task, and repeated runs define the prior-weighted task average. Classicality is imposed only by requiring the Hamiltonian settings of the same device to commute. The paper derives the corresponding classical average-work law and shows that incompatible Hamiltonian settings...</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** The paper proves that non-commuting Hamiltonian settings allow for a higher average work extraction across multiple processes than any possible commuting (classical) device. It establishes a new thermodynamic law and identifies Hamiltonian incompatibility as a fundamental resource for work extraction.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for researchers in open quantum systems and thermodynamics as it identifies a new way to certify quantum advantage using thermodynamic quantities rather than Bell inequalities, and treats non-commutativity as a quantifiable resource.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Determining whether Hamiltonian incompatibility (non-commutativity) acts as a thermodynamic resource to extract more average work across multiple tasks than any classical (commuting) device can achieve.

**Main result.** The authors derive a universal classical average-work law and prove that incompatible Hamiltonians can exceed this limit, establishing Hamiltonian incompatibility as a fundamental thermodynamic resource.

**Method.** The study uses a thermodynamic framework involving nonequilibrium free-energy differences, quantum relative entropy, and geometric optimization over tracial noncommuting polynomials and Bloch-sphere geometries.

**Model / system.** A work-extraction task involving a black-box device queried with bounded Hamiltonians (0 <= H <= I) using a source of pure qubit preparations constrained by pairwise maximal-energy data.

**Key observables.** Average work (W_p), average-work advantage (Delta_av), and visibility (v).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Hamiltonian commutativity, visibility threshold (v_c), source geometry (theta), and reference energy averages (mu_j).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The preparations are assumed to be pure, and the work device is treated as a black box with no specific microscopic model or dimension restriction.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates the work-extraction task, showing the flow from the constrained source to the work device and comparing the free-energy envelope to the commutativity constraint.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the work-extraction task, establishes the branch-wise free-energy benchmark, derives the classical average-work law for a minimal task, quantifies the quantum advantage, and analyzes the robustness of this advantage against noise and task complexity.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Free energy fixes the maximum work of a thermodynamic process once the state and Hamiltonian are specified. A work-extraction task asks a different question: how much average work can a single device realize across several preparations and Hamiltonian settings? A classical work device is one whose Hamiltonian settings are mutually commuting. We place every branch at its best free-energy-limited work envelope and derive the corresponding classical limit on the task average. For pure preparations, the source is specified only by pairwise maximal-energy constraints: for each pair, the intrinsic maximal average energy under one common normalized Hamiltonian is bounded as part of the task data, while the work device is otherwise microscopically unrestricted. The benchmark is optimized over arbitrary-dimensional classical implementations. Incompatible Hamiltonian settings exceed this limit, even though every branch remains bounded by its own free-energy maximum. The advantage therefore does not arise in any single process, but in the average work of the task: incompatible Hamiltonians realize a value that no classical work device can attain. Hamiltonian incompatibility is thus a thermodynamic resource for work extraction.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.03404"></a>
### [Sparkling bubbles in chiral active fluids](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.03404v1)

**Authors:** Alessandro Petrini, Raphaël Maire, Umberto Marini Bettolo Marconi, Lorenzo Caprini  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.03404v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
